- `github.com/sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy TLS Certificate Validation Pipeline

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement TLS certificate validation. Identify: the abstract CertValidator interface, the DefaultCertValidator with X.509 chain verification, the SAN matcher for Subject Alternative Name matching (DNS, URI, email, IP), the ContextImpl managing TLS certificates and OCSP responses, and the OCSP response parsing and stapling support.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

## Summary of Findings

I've created a comprehensive JSON file at `/workspace/answer.json` documenting all the C++ source files implementing TLS certificate validation in Envoy v1.31.2:

### **Key Components Identified:**

1. **Abstract CertValidator Interface** (`source/common/tls/cert_validator/cert_validator.h`)
   - Pure virtual interface with methods for certificate validation, context initialization, and session ID hashing

2. **DefaultCertValidator** (X.509 Chain Verification)
   - Implements standard X.509 certificate chain validation using BoringSSL
   - Supports certificate pinning (hash and SPKI), CRL handling, and untrusted certificate modes

3. **SAN Matcher** (Subject Alternative Name Validation)
   - StringSanMatcher class supporting multiple SAN types: DNS, URI, EMAIL, IP, and custom OIDs
   - Flexible pattern matching (exact, regex, prefix, suffix)
   - Factory function `createStringSanMatcher()` for dynamic instantiation

4. **ContextImpl** (TLS Context Management)
   - Base class managing SSL contexts and certificate validators
   - ClientContextImpl and ServerContextImpl specializations
   - Handles asynchronous certificate validation callbacks
   - Manages OCSP response storage and expiration

5. **OCSP Response Support**
   - Complete OCSP (RFC 6960) implementation with ASN.1 parsing
   - OcspResponseWrapperImpl for managing DER-encoded responses
   - BasicOcspResponse for standard OCSP response format
   - OCSP stapling with three policies: Lenient, Strict, and MustStaple

6. **SPIFFE Validator** (Alternative Implementation)
   - Extends CertValidator for SPIFFE-based trust domains
   - Trust bundle management and

SAN Matcher (Subject Alternative Name Matching)\\n**Files**: `source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.h`, `.cc`\\n\\nImplements flexible Subject Alternative Name matching:\\n- **SanMatcher Interface**: Pure virtual `match()` method for checking if a GENERAL_NAME matches criteria\\n- **StringSanMatcher Class**: Concrete implementation supporting multiple SAN types:\\n  - `GEN_DNS`: Domain name matching with wildcard support and regex patterns\\n  - `GEN_URI`: URI matching\\n  - `GEN_EMAIL`: Email address matching\\n  - `GEN_IPADD`: IP address matching\\n  - `GEN_OTHERNAME`: OID-based \\\"Other Name\\\" matching with custom ASN.1 objects\\n- **createStringSanMatcher()**: Factory function that creates appropriate matchers based on `SubjectAltNameMatcher` protobuf configuration\\n- Uses `StringMatcherImpl` for flexible pattern matching (exact, prefix, suffix, regex, contains)\\n\\n## 4. ContextImpl (TLS Context Management)\\n**Files**: \\n- `source/common/tls/context_impl.h`, `.cc`: Base implementation\\n- `source/common/tls/client_context_impl.h`, `.cc`: Client-side specialization\\n- `source/common/tls/server_context_impl.h`, `.cc`: Server-side specialization\\n\\nThe `ContextImpl` class manages:\\n- **TLS Contexts**: Maintains `std::vector<Ssl::TlsContext> tls_contexts_` where each contains:\\n  - `ssl_ctx_`: BoringSSL SSL_CTX\\n  - `cert_chain_`: X509 certificate chain\\n  - `ocsp_response_`: Unique OCSP response wrapper\\n  - `is_ecdsa_`, `is_must_staple_`: Certificate properties\\n- **Certificate Validator**: Holds `CertValidatorPtr cert_validator_` for performing validations\\n- **Custom Verify Callback**: Static `customVerifyCallback()` for asynchronous certificate validation\\n- **OCSP Support**: `secondsUntilFirstOcspResponseExpires()` queries OCSP response expiration\\n- **Asynchronous Validation**: `customVerifyCertChain()` and `customVerifyCertChainForQuic()` for async cert validation\\n\\nServerContextImpl additionally handles:\\n- OCSP stapling with policies (Lenient, Strict, Must Staple)\\n- `ocspStapleAction()`: Determines whether to staple OCSP response based on client capabilities\\n- Server Name Indication (SNI) based certificate selection\\n- TLS context selection via `selectTlsContext()` and `findTlsContext()` methods\\n\\n## 5. SPIFFE Validator (Alternative Implementation)\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/cert_validator/spiffe/spiffe_validator.h`, `.cc`\\n\\nAlternative CertValidator implementation for SPIFFE (Secure Production Identity Framework For Everyone):\\n- Extends CertValidator interface for trust bundle-based validation\\n- `trustBundleStores()`: Maintains per-trust-domain X509_STORE for verification\\n- `extractTrustDomain()`: Parses SPIFFE identity from URI SANs\\n- `certificatePrecheck()`: Validates certificate structure before chain verification\\n- `matchSubjectAltName()`: Uses SAN matchers for SPIFFE-specific validation\\n- Supports expired certificate allowance for testing\\n\\n## Integration Flow\\n\\nThe complete pipeline works as follows:\\n1. **Initialization**: ContextImpl creates a CertValidator (typically DefaultCertValidator) and calls `initializeSslContexts()`\\n2. **Handshake**: During TLS handshake, OpenSSL invokes the custom verify callback registered with `SSL_CTX_set_custom_verify()`\\n3. **Validation**: ContextImpl's `customVerifyCallback()` delegates to `doVerifyCertChain()` on the CertValidator\\n4. **Chain Verification**: DefaultCertValidator performs X.509 chain validation using X509_STORE_CTX\\n5. **SAN Matching**: After chain verification, StringSanMatchers validate the certificate's Subject Alternative Names\\n6. **Async Handling**: For async validators, ValidateResultCallback is invoked when validation completes\\n7. **OCSP Support**: ServerContextImpl manages OCSP responses, checking expiration via OcspResponseWrapperImpl\\n8. **Result**: ValidationResults with status and error details are returned to the SSL library\\n\\nThis architecture provides a flexible, pluggable certificate validation system supporting standard X.509 validation, SPIFFE identity verification, OCSP stapling, and custom validation logic.\"\n}\n",

SAN Matcher (Subject Alternative Name Matching)\\n**Files**: `source/common/tls/cert_validator/san_matcher.h`, `.cc`\\n\\nImplements flexible Subject Alternative Name matching:\\n- **SanMatcher Interface**: Pure virtual `match()` method for checking if a GENERAL_NAME matches criteria\\n- **StringSanMatcher Class**: Concrete implementation supporting multiple SAN types:\\n  - `GEN_DNS`: Domain name matching with wildcard support and regex patterns\\n  - `GEN_URI`: URI matching\\n  - `GEN_EMAIL`: Email address matching\\n  - `GEN_IPADD`: IP address matching\\n  - `GEN_OTHERNAME`: OID-based \\\"Other Name\\\" matching with custom ASN.1 objects\\n- **createStringSanMatcher()**: Factory function that creates appropriate matchers based on `SubjectAltNameMatcher` protobuf configuration\\n- Uses `StringMatcherImpl` for flexible pattern matching (exact, prefix, suffix, regex, contains)\\n\\n## 4. ContextImpl (TLS Context Management)\\n**Files**: \\n- `source/common/tls/context_impl.h`, `.cc`: Base implementation\\n- `source/common/tls/client_context_impl.h`, `.cc`: Client-side specialization\\n- `source/common/tls/server_context_impl.h`, `.cc`: Server-side specialization\\n\\nThe `ContextImpl` class manages:\\n- **TLS Contexts**: Maintains `std::vector<Ssl::TlsContext> tls_contexts_` where each contains:\\n  - `ssl_ctx_`: BoringSSL SSL_CTX\\n  - `cert_chain_`: X509 certificate chain\\n  - `ocsp_response_`: Unique OCSP response wrapper\\n  - `is_ecdsa_`, `is_must_staple_`: Certificate properties\\n- **Certificate Validator**: Holds `CertValidatorPtr cert_validator_` for performing validations\\n- **Custom Verify Callback**: Static `customVerifyCallback()` for asynchronous certificate validation\\n- **OCSP Support**: `secondsUntilFirstOcspResponseExpires()` queries OCSP response expiration\\n- **Asynchronous Validation**: `customVerifyCertChain()` and `customVerifyCertChainForQuic()` for async cert validation\\n\\nServerContextImpl additionally handles:\\n- OCSP stapling with policies (Lenient, Strict, Must Staple)\\n- `ocspStapleAction()`: Determines whether to staple OCSP response based on client capabilities\\n- Server Name Indication (SNI) based certificate selection\\n- TLS context selection via `selectTlsContext()` and `findTlsContext()` methods\\n\\n## 5. SPIFFE Validator (Alternative Implementation)\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/transport_sockets/tls/cert_validator/spiffe/spiffe_validator.h`, `.cc`\\n\\nAlternative CertValidator implementation for SPIFFE (Secure Production Identity Framework For Everyone):\\n- Extends CertValidator interface for trust bundle-based validation\\n- `trustBundleStores()`: Maintains per-trust-domain X509_STORE for verification\\n- `extractTrustDomain()`: Parses SPIFFE identity from URI SANs\\n- `certificatePrecheck()`: Validates certificate structure before chain verification\\n- `matchSubjectAltName()`: Uses SAN matchers for SPIFFE-specific validation\\n- Supports expired certificate allowance for testing\\n\\n## Integration Flow\\n\\nThe complete pipeline works as follows:\\n1. **Initialization**: ContextImpl creates a CertValidator (typically DefaultCertValidator) and calls `initializeSslContexts()`\\n2. **Handshake**: During TLS handshake, OpenSSL invokes the custom verify callback registered with `SSL_CTX_set_custom_verify()`\\n3. **Validation**: ContextImpl's `customVerifyCallback()` delegates to `doVerifyCertChain()` on the CertValidator\\n4. **Chain Verification**: DefaultCertValidator performs X.509 chain validation using X509_STORE_CTX\\n5. **SAN Matching**: After chain verification, StringSanMatchers validate the certificate's Subject Alternative Names\\n6. **Async Handling**: For async validators, ValidateResultCallback is invoked when validation completes\\n7. **OCSP Support**: ServerContextImpl manages OCSP responses, checking expiration via OcspResponseWrapperImpl\\n8. **Result**: ValidationResults with status and error details are returned to the SSL library\\n\\nThis architecture provides a flexible, pluggable certificate validation system supporting standard X.509 validation, SPIFFE identity verification, OCSP stapling, and custom validation logic.\"\n}\n",
